+{"parentUuid":"931e1240-2bb2-472b-a081-790ebaa47c90","isSidechain":false,"teamName":"gtd-evolution","userType":"external","cwd":"/home/jwilger/projects/todo_list","sessionId":"9823e89e-4a23-4ccc-9757-1b9bb393ba5c","version":"2.1.39","gitBranch":"main","slug":"jolly-snuggling-giraffe","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":"<teammate-message teammate_id=\"steve-schoger\" color=\"cyan\">\n{\"type\":\"idle_notification\",\"from\":\"steve-schoger\",\"timestamp\":\"2026-02-11T19:30:28.387Z\",\"idleReason\":\"available\"}\n</teammate-message>\n\n<teammate-message teammate_id=\"heydon-pickering\" color=\"blue\" summary=\"Retro input: calibrate severity, codify accessible names, honest SR testing\">\n## Retrospective Input -- Heydon Pickering (Accessibility)\n\n### What Went Well\n\n1. **Accessibility is being caught early, not bolted on.** The delete button `aria-label` issue in Task #15 was caught in review and fixed before shipping. The nested nav landmark issue in Task #11 was flagged (even if I initially over-weighted it). This is the model working -- a11y review as a continuous quality gate, not an afterthought.\n\n2. **axe-core in the e2e tests is paying dividends.** It caught the contrast bug in `--color-primary` during polish, and it's now routinely scanning every new page (empty state AND populated state). The team has internalized this pattern -- Luca added axe-core scanning for the inbox page without being asked.\n\n3. **Accessible patterns are becoming team habits.** `aria-live` announcements for HTMX swaps, visible labels on all inputs, `aria-current=\"page\"` on nav links, `role=\"list\"` on styled lists, semantic `<ul>` for item collections -- these are now automatic. The team doesn't need me to remind them of the basics.\n\n4. **Product discovery included accessibility from the start.** The user stories have dedicated \"Accessibility\" sections with specific criteria. Marty and the team accepted my input on clarify flow (progressive disclosure vs wizard), navigation patterns (single nav, no sidebar), and interaction patterns for all GTD views. This is how it should work -- accessibility shapes the design, it doesn't audit it afterwards.\n\n5. **The \"approve with one blocking fix\" pattern works well.** In Task #15, I had one blocking issue (delete button labels) and one non-blocking note (discarded error message). This granularity lets the team understand what's a showstopper vs what's a refinement. In Task #11 I initially flagged 3 issues as blocking and then re-evaluated them as non-blocking for a skeleton -- learning to calibrate severity for the current stage.\n\n### What Went Poorly\n\n1. **I was too strict on Task #11 (skeleton review).** I initially blocked on three issues that were all non-blocking for a skeleton page. The nested nav is not ideal but not broken. Dashboard links and units on placeholder zeros are premature. Quick capture form-level aria-label is a refinement. I wasted team time by not calibrating my review to the stage of the work. A skeleton doesn't need the same scrutiny as a finished feature.\n\n2. **Accessibility acceptance criteria in user stories could be more specific about what \"keyboard operable\" means.** Every story says \"All interactive elements are fully keyboard operable\" but doesn't specify Tab order, Enter/Space behavior, or Escape handling for specific patterns. When we get to the clarify form with its conditional fields, this will matter. I should have pushed for more specific keyboard interaction specs during discovery.\n\n3. **No way to verify screen reader behavior in CI.** The Definition of Done says \"Screen reader testing (VoiceOver, NVDA, or equivalent) confirms...\" but we have no automated screen reader testing. axe-core catches structural issues but not announcement quality, focus order after dynamic updates, or live region timing. This is a known gap in the industry, but we should acknowledge it rather than pretend the checkbox is checked.\n\n### Proposed Changes\n\n**1. TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md -- Add accessible name checklist to Definition of Done (Accessibility section):**\n\nAdd a bullet under the existing accessibility checklist:\n```\n- [ ] All interactive elements (buttons, links) have unique accessible names that\n      include the item they act on (e.g., \"Delete: Buy groceries\", not just \"Delete\")\n```\n\nThis codifies what we already know from US-7 and the inbox delete button fix. It's the pattern that keeps coming up.\n\n**2. TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md -- Clarify screen reader testing reality:**\n\nChange the current bullet:\n```\n- [ ] Screen reader testing (VoiceOver, NVDA, or equivalent) confirms: interactive\n      elements are announced correctly, state changes are communicated, and dynamic\n      content updates are announced via live regions\n```\nTo:\n```\n- [ ] Structural accessibility verified via axe-core automated scanning (covers ~30%\n      of WCAG). Manual screen reader testing (VoiceOver, NVDA) performed for new\n      interaction patterns (modals, live regions, focus management). Routine pages\n      covered by axe-core are not required to have manual SR testing on every change.\n```\n\nThis is honest about what we can actually verify and avoids pretending we do full manual SR testing on every commit.\n\n**3. On the mini-retro after every CI build:**\n\nI support this for process adherence. From my perspective, the a11y-relevant question is: \"Did axe-core run on the new/changed pages?\" If not, that's a gap to fix before moving on.\n\n**4. On session transcript CI triggers:**\n\nThese should be excluded. They contain no code changes and waste CI resources. A `.github/workflows` path filter or a `[skip ci]` convention for transcript-only commits would handle this.\n</teammate-message>\n\n<teammate-message teammate_id=\"lea-verou\" color=\"pink\" summary=\"Retro input: 7 positives, 5 concerns, 4 proposed changes\">\nLea Verou -- Retrospective Input (Tasks #1, #11, #15)\n\n## What Went Well\n\n1. **CSS architecture held up beautifully through GTD evolution.** The cascade layers + design token system we established in the MVP scaled naturally to the new GTD components (`.gtd-nav`, `.inbox-item`, `.dashboard__stat`, `.quick-capture`). Every new component used tokens exclusively -- no hardcoded values crept in. This validates the upfront investment in the token system.\n\n2. **Team design consensus process worked.** The sidebar vs. header nav debate (Task #1) was a genuine architectural decision with strong opinions on multiple sides. We resolved it through structured discussion -- Heydon's a11y pushback, Carson's scope argument, Steve Krug's visual hierarchy reframing, and Steve Schoger gracefully dropping his sidebar proposal. The outcome (wrapping header nav) was better than any individual's initial proposal.\n\n3. **BEM naming consistency.** New components consistently follow BEM conventions (`inbox-item__title`, `gtd-nav__link`, `dashboard__stat`). No naming drift across tasks.\n\n4. **Progressive enhancement is real, not aspirational.** Every feature works without JavaScript. HTMX enhances. We need to track deferred a11y items explicitly and address them before they compound.\n\n4. **Review feedback sometimes duplicated across reviewers.** I sent Luca detailed CSS review, then discovered Heydon and Steve had already flagged overlapping items. We could be more efficient by reading each other's reviews before writing our own. The pipeline says: code -> fmt -> clippy -> test -> commit -> push -> **CI GREEN** -> next step. We pushed 4 commits in ~12 minutes while each CI run takes ~5 minutes. This means we had 3-4 CI runs queued simultaneously.\n\n   **Root cause from my perspective**: As the Driver, I was focused on making progress through the implementation steps. The pipeline felt slow (5+ minutes per CI run) and I prioritized velocity over discipline. This was wrong. The whole point of the pipeline is to catch issues early. If a CI run fails on commit 2 but we've already pushed commits 3 and 4, we have a mess.\n\n2. **Driver context loss across respawns.** I was spawned multiple times during this task. Each respawn required re-reading all project files, understanding what had already been built, and figuring out where to pick up. This is inherently lossy -- I missed the fact that a previous Luca instance had already partially implemented the feature until I read the source files. The session transcripts help but they're not a perfect substitute for continuous context.\n\n3. **Stale server causing false test failures.** I spent significant time debugging Playwright tests that were failing because they were connecting to a stale server running old compiled code. The `reuseExistingServer: !process.env.CI` setting in `playwright.config.ts` makes this easy to hit. When a background server from a previous run is still alive, Playwright happily connects to it even though the code has changed.\n\n4. **Dead code shipped (`user_facing` variable).** The too-long title error message is computed but discarded at `src/routes/inbox.rs:135`. This means users submitting a too-long title via no-JS get a 422 page with no explanation. Three reviewers flagged this independently (Kent, Heydon, me), which suggests it's a real gap. We should have wired it up in-task rather than deferring.\n\n5. **Test helper duplication.** The `register_and_login` helper is now duplicated across multiple test files. This wasn't introduced by this task -- it's accumulating technical debt. Each new feature copies the pattern rather than extracting it.\n\n### Proposed Changes\n\n**1. TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md -- Strengthen pipeline enforcement:**\n\nAdd to Section \"Atomic Green Step Pipeline\" (after step 10):\n\n```markdown\n### Pipeline Timing Rules\n- **Wait for CI before pushing the next commit.** Run `gh run watch` or poll \n  `gh run list --limit 1` until the current CI run completes before pushing again.\n- **If you have local green but CI hasn't finished the previous run**, stop and wait.\n  Use the time to review your own code, write documentation, or plan the next step.\n- **Never have more than 1 pending CI run at a time.** If `gh run list` shows an \n  in_progress run, do not push.\n```\n\n**2. TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md -- Add Driver handoff protocol:**\n\nAdd a new subsection under \"Driver-Reviewer Mob Model\":\n\n```markdown\n### Driver Handoff Protocol\nWhen a Driver is respawned (due to context loss, rotation, or session restart):\n1. The coordinator provides a written summary of: what has been completed, what \n   remains, and where to find the relevant code.\n2. The new Driver reads the summary AND runs `git log --oneline -10` and \n   `git diff HEAD` before writing any code.\n3. The new Driver runs the full pipeline (fmt + clippy + test + playwright) to \n   verify the current state is green before making changes.\n4. The new Driver sends a \"ready\" message to the coordinator confirming they have \n   context and a green baseline.\n```\n\n**3. I could have been more proactive about verifying TDD discipline in real-time.** I sent TDD guidance at the start of each task and reviewed at the end, but I didn't check intermediate commits for test-first discipline. The separation of concerns means domain logic stays pure and testable without mocking.\n\n3. **Type-driven design prevented bugs.** Separate `InboxItemId` newtype (not reusing `TodoItemId`), `InboxItem` as a struct (not an enum -- no state transitions), authorization checks before mutations -- these are all patterns we established in design review that were correctly implemented. The type system carries the domain rules.\n\n4. **Cross-discipline review caught real issues.** The product discovery phase benefited enormously from having all 9 perspectives. For example: Heydon corrected my stale assumption about the clarify flow (wizard vs single form), Steve Krug was convinced by domain reasoning to include contexts in Phase 1, and Marty's argument about migration (pending todos -> inbox for onboarding value) was better than my original suggestion (pending -> NextAction).\n\n5. **Comprehensive test coverage from TDD.** 99 Rust tests + 9 Playwright e2e tests after just two implementation steps. The tests read like behavior specs, and axe-core catches real a11y issues.\n\n### What Went Poorly\n\n1. **Naming departures from the glossary went unchallenged during implementation.** I recommended `InboxItem::capture()` instead of `::new()`, `captured_at` instead of `created_at`, and `ItemTitle` instead of `TodoTitle`. All three were documented in the glossary. Luca used the more generic names. I flagged these as non-blocking in my review, but this creates a gap between the glossary (our source of truth for ubiquitous language) and the actual code. The whole point of a ubiquitous language is that it's used everywhere -- including constructor names and field names.\n\n2. **Atomic Green Step pipeline violations.** Multiple commits pushed without waiting for CI green on each. This violates the pipeline we agreed on. The pipeline exists because a failing CI that was never checked between commits makes it harder to identify which change broke things. Each commit should be a known-good state.\n\n3. **Driver restarts lost context.** When Luca was respawned between tasks, he sometimes had stale context about what had already been decided. My domain guidance messages had to repeat information that was already in the glossary and product discovery documents. This is wasteful -- the documents should be the single source of truth, and the Driver should read them at the start of each task.\n\n4. **Review consensus was sometimes ceremonial rather than substantive.** With 9 reviewers, there's a risk that some reviews are \"LGTM\" rubber stamps rather than deep reviews from the reviewer's area of expertise. I try to make my domain reviews substantive, but I'm not sure all reviewers are catching issues in their specialty areas.\n\n### Proposed Changes\n\n**1. TEAM_AGREEMENTS.md -- Add \"Ubiquitous Language Enforcement\" to the Atomic Green Step Pipeline**\n\nAdd after step 5 (playwright test):\n> **5b. Definition of Done\n    81→\n    82→A feature is **done** when ALL of the following are true:\n    83→\n    84→### Product\n    85→- [ ] The user problem is clearly solved\n    86→- [ ] All acceptance criteria from the user story are met\n    87→- [ ] A first-time user can accomplish the task without hesitating (Trunk Test)\n    88→- [ ] User can complete a full journey from the landing page through the feature\n    89→      being delivered\n    90→- [ ] All navigation paths lead somewhere useful (no dead-end pages)\n    91→- [ ] Edge cases are handled gracefully (not just the happy path)\n    92→- [ ] The feature is deployable -- not just merged, but shippable to real users\n    93→\n    94→### Engineering\n    95→- [ ] Tests are written first (TDD: Red-Green-Refactor) and all pass\n    96→- [ ] `cargo fmt --check` passes\n    97→- [ ] `cargo clippy -- -D warnings` passes with zero warnings\n    98→- [ ] `cargo test` passes (unit + integration)\n    99→- [ ] `npx playwright test` passes -- browser-based e2e tests pass for affected\n   100→      user flows\n   101→- [ ] Error cases return meaningful HTML responses with structured logging\n   102→- [ ] Tracing spans cover the new functionality\n   103→- [ ] Database migrations (if any) are committed and `sqlx-data.json` is updated\n   104→\n   105→### Accessibility (WCAG 2.2 AA)\n   106→- [ ] HTML is semantic and uses correct elements (`<button>`, `<label>`, `<ul>`, etc.)\n   107→- [ ] All form inputs have visible `<label>` elements (no placeholder-only inputs)\n   108→- [ ] All interactive elements are fully keyboard operable\n   109→- [ ] Screen reader testing (VoiceOver, NVDA, or equivalent) confirms: interactive\n   110→      elements are announced correctly, state changes are communicated, and dynamic\n   111→      content updates are announced via live regions\n   112→- [ ] ARIA used only when native HTML semantics are insufficient (with comments explaining why)\n   113→- [ ] Color contrast meets WCAG AA (4.5:1 for normal text, 3:1 for large text/UI)\n   114→- [ ] Color is never the only indicator of state (always a secondary visual cue)\n   115→- [ ] Focus management is correct after HTMX swaps (see HTMX Focus Protocol below)\n   116→- [ ] Custom `:focus-visible` styles are present with sufficient contrast\n   117→- [ ] `prefers-reduced-motion` is respected for all animations/transitions\n   118→\n   119→### Design\n   120→- [ ] Visual design follows the established design token system\n   121→- [ ] All states are designed: empty, loading, error, success\n   122→- [ ] Visual hierarchy is clear -- one primary focal point per screen\n   123→- [ ] Spacing is consistent and uses the defined scale\n   124→\n   125→### Frontend\n   126→- [ ] Core functionality works via standard HTML forms and links (progressive\n   127→      enhancement -- HTMX and TypeScript enhance but are not required for basic operation)\n   128→- [ ] HTMX attributes follow locality of behavior (self-describing elements)\n   129→- [ ] TypeScript (if any) is non-critical and has accessible alternatives\n   130→\n   131→### Process\n   132→- [ ] The mob has continuously reviewed code, design, usability, and accessibility\n   133→      during development\n   134→- [ ] All 9 team members have reviewed and consent to the completed work\n   135→- [ ] Labels and copy follow the Copy Standards (see Section 3)\n   136→\n   137→---\n   138→\n   139→## 3. Code Conventions and Patterns\n   140→\n   141→### Project Structure\n   142→\n   143→```\n   144→src/\n   145→  main.rs              -- Startup, configuration loading, server binding\n   146→  lib.rs               -- Re-exports for integration test access\n   147→  configuration.rs     -- Config structs, environment-aware loading\n   148→  startup.rs           -- Application builder (Router, DB pool, middleware)\n   149→  routes/              -- HTTP handlers (thin: extract, delegate, respond)\n   150→    mod.rs\n   151→    health_check.rs\n   152→  domain/              -- Pure domain types and logic (NO I/O)\n   153→    mod.rs\n   154→  services/            -- Application services (orchestrate domain + infra)\n   155→    mod.rs\n   156→  infrastructure/      -- Database queries, external service clients\n   157→    mod.rs\n   158→  templates/           -- Askama HTML templates\n   159→tests/\n   160→  api/                 -- Integration tests against the full HTTP stack\n   161→    mod.rs\n   162→    helpers.rs         -- TestApp, spawn_app(), shared fixtures\n   163→    health_check.rs\n   164→```\n   165→\n   166→Dependencies flow inward: routes -> services -> domain + infrastructure.\n   167→Domain depends on nothing. This makes the domain layer trivially testable.\n   168→\n   169→### Rust Conventions\n   170→\n   171→**Type-driven domain modeling:**\n   172→- Newtypes for all domain identifiers and constrained values: `UserId(Uuid)`,\n   173→  `Email(String)`, `Title(String)`, `TodoItemId(Uuid)`\n   174→- Enums for state machines -- make illegal states unrepresentable:\n   175→  ```rust\n   176→  // GOOD: the type system prevents invalid states\n   177→  enum TodoItem {\n   178→      Pending { title: Title, created_at: DateTime<Utc> },\n   179→      Completed { title: Title, created_at: DateTime<Utc>, completed_at: DateTime<Utc> },\n   180→  }\n   181→  ```\n   182→- **Parse, don't validate**: Instead of `fn validate(input: &str) -> bool`, write\n   183→  `fn parse(input: String) -> Result<Email, ValidationError>`. Validation that returns\n   184→  a boolean throws away information. Parsing produces a typed value that carries the\n   185→  proof of validity. Validate once at the boundary; never re-validate inside the system.\n   186→\n   187→**Workflows as type-safe pipelines:**\n   188→```\n   189→UnvalidatedInput -> ValidatedInput -> DomainEvent -> PersistenceResult\n   190→```\n   191→Each step's output type is the next step's input. You cannot skip validation or\n   192→persist before validating.\n   193→\n   194→**Error handling (three layers):**\n   195→- **Domain errors**: Custom enum with `thiserror`. Domain terms only -- no HTTP concepts,\n   196→  no infrastructure types. A `TodoError::TitleEmpty` must never contain a `sqlx::Error`.\n   197→  Domain errors and infrastructure errors are separate types, translated at the boundary.\n   198→  ```rust\n   199→  #[derive(Debug, thiserror::Error)]\n   200→  pub enum TodoError {\n   201→      #[error(\"Todo title cannot be empty\")]\n   202→      TitleEmpty,\n   203→      #[error(\"Todo title too long (max {max}, got {actual})\")]\n   204→      TitleTooLong { max: usize, actual: usize },\n   205→      #[error(\"Todo not found\")]\n   206→      NotFound { id: TodoItemId },\n   207→      #[error(transparent)]\n   208→      Unexpected(#[from] anyhow::Error),\n   209→  }\n   210→  ```\n   211→- **Service errors**: Map domain errors to actionable responses. Add context.\n   212→- **Route errors**: Implement `IntoResponse` for error types. Return meaningful HTML\n   213→  (not raw 500s). Every error path produces a user-facing response.\n   214→- **Always add context** when propagating errors. A bare `?` that loses context is a\n   215→  code smell.\n   216→- **Log at error boundaries**: Every error crossing an architectural boundary gets\n   217→  logged with structured `tracing` fields.\n   218→\n   219→**Idiomatic Rust:**\n   220→- Prefer iterators over loops, pattern matching over conditionals\n   221→- `?` operator for error propagation with context\n   222→- `#[must_use]` on important return types\n   223→- Compile-time guarantees: SQLx `query!`/`query_as!` macros, Askama templates\n   224→\n   225→**Testing strategy (TDD):**\n   226→- **Unit tests** (`#[cfg(test)] mod tests`): Pure domain logic, validation, type\n   227→  conversions. Fast, no I/O, no mocking. **Litmus test: if you need a mock to test\n   228→  domain logic, I/O has leaked into the domain layer. Push it back to the boundary.**\n   229→- **Integration tests** (`tests/` directory): Full HTTP stack with real database.\n   230→  `TestApp` struct with `spawn_app()` helper. Unique database per test run\n   231→  (random name, run migrations, drop after).\n   232→- **No mocks for the database**: Use real PostgreSQL via Docker. Mocks give false\n   233→  confidence.\n   234→- **Test names as behavior specifications**:\n   235→  ```rust\n   236→  #[tokio::test]\n   237→  async fn registration_returns_422_when_email_is_missing() { ... }\n   238→  ```\n   239→- **Acceptance tests as usability statements**: \"When I type a todo and press Enter,\n   240→  it appears in my list.\" Tests describe what the user expects to happen.\n   241→- **Property-based tests** with `proptest` where appropriate.\n   242→- **End-to-end tests** (`e2e/` directory): Playwright browser tests against the\n   243→  running application. Cover critical user journeys (register, login, core feature,\n   244→  logout). Use role-based and label-based locators (`getByRole`, `getByLabel`) so\n   245→  tests double as accessibility assertions. Keep this layer thin -- only add e2e\n   246→  tests for flows that integration tests cannot adequately verify.\n   247→- **Accessibility testing** (four layers):\n   248→  - *Automated*: axe-core (or equivalent) in the test suite for missing labels,\n   249→    contrast violations, and structural issues\n   250→  - *Keyboard*: Manual keyboard navigation testing for every interactive flow\n   251→  - *Screen reader*: Manual VoiceOver/NVDA testing for every feature\n   252→  - *Structural*: HTML validation for semantic correctness\n   253→  Tests can assert on roles, labels, and ARIA attributes -- documenting the expected\n   254→  screen reader experience as living specifications.\n   255→\n   256→### Initial Crate List\n   257→\n   258→Proposed starting dependencies (open to mob discussion):\n   259→\n   260→| Crate | Purpose |\n   261→|-------|---------|\n   262→| `axum` | Web framework |\n   263→| `tokio` (full features) | Async runtime |\n   264→| `sqlx` (postgres, migrate, runtime-tokio-rustls) | Database |\n   265→| `askama` + `askama_axum` | Templates |\n   266→| `serde` + `serde_json` | Serialization |\n   267→| `tracing` + `tracing-subscriber` (env-filter) | Observability |\n   268→| `thiserror` | Domain error types |\n   269→| `anyhow` | Ad-hoc error context |\n   270→| `argon2` | Password hashing |\n   271→| `tower-sessions` + `tower-sessions-sqlx-store` | Session management |\n   272→| `uuid` | Identifiers |\n   273→\n   274→Note: Input validation will be handled through custom newtypes with validation in\n   275→constructors (Scott's approach), not a validation framework. The types carry the\n   276→proof of validity.\n   277→\n   278→### HTML / HTMX Conventions\n   279→\n   280→**The Hypermedia Contract:**\n   281→- **Return HTML, not JSON.** Every UI endpoint returns HTML. No JSON API layer.\n   282→- **Semantic HTML first**: `<button>` for actions, `<a>` for navigation, `<form>` for\n   283→  data submission, `<ul>`/`<ol>` for lists. Never `<div onclick>`.\n   284→- **Form accessibility**: Every input has a visible `<label>` (never placeholder-only).\n   285→  Validation errors are associated with inputs via `aria-describedby` and announced\n   286→  via `aria-live=\"polite\"` regions. Use `aria-live=\"assertive\"` only for critical errors.\n   287→- **Locality of behavior**: Every HTMX-enhanced element is self-describing. You\n   288→  understand what it does by looking at it alone.\n   289→- **No client-side state**: The DOM is the state, the server is the source of truth.\n   290→  No client-side data stores. The only acceptable client-side state is transient UI\n   291→  state for progressive enhancement (e.g., drag position).\n   292→\n   293→**Server endpoint conventions:**\n   294→- **Full page requests** (no `HX-Request` header): Return complete HTML page with\n   295→  layout, nav, landmarks.\n   296→- **HTMX requests** (with `HX-Request` header): Return just the HTML fragment for\n   297→  the swap.\n   298→- **`HX-Trigger` response header** for cross-component updates (e.g., updating a\n   299→  todo count after deletion).\n   300→- **Same URL, same handler**: One handler checks the `HX-Request` header to decide\n   301→  whether to return a full page or a fragment. No separate `/api/` routes.\n   302→- **HTTP methods used semantically**: GET = read, POST = create, PUT/PATCH = update,\n   303→  DELETE = delete.\n   304→- **Status codes**: 200 for success with HTML, 422 for validation errors with error\n   305→  HTML, 200 with empty body for deletion (allows HTMX swap to remove element).\n   306→\n   307→**Progressive enhancement (non-negotiable):**\n   308→- The app MUST work without JavaScript. Forms submit, links navigate, content is\n   309→  readable with HTML alone.\n   310→- HTMX enhances the experience (partial updates, no full page reloads).\n   311→- TypeScript is only for things neither HTML nor HTMX can do.\n   312→\n   313→**HTMX Focus Management Protocol:**\n   314→After every HTMX swap:\n   315→- If an element was **removed**: Move focus to the logical next element.\n   316→- If content was **updated in place**: Keep focus where it was.\n   317→- Use `aria-live=\"polite\"` regions to announce state changes to screen readers.\n   318→- Test every HTMX interaction with Tab key before considering it done.\n   319→\n   320→**Page structure (every page):**\n   321→- Skip link to main content (first focusable element)\n   322→- Landmark regions: `<main>`, `<nav>`, `<header>`, `<footer>`\n   323→- Logical heading hierarchy: one `<h1>` per page, no skipped levels\n   324→- Descriptive `<title>` element\n   325→\n   326→### CSS Conventions\n   327→\n   328→**Progressive enhancement layers:**\n   329→1. **Layer 1 (HTML)**: Functional and readable with zero CSS.\n   330→2. **Layer 2 (CSS)**: Beautiful -- layout, typography, color, transitions, focus styles.\n   331→3. **Layer 3 (TypeScript)**: Delightful -- drag-and-drop, advanced keyboard shortcuts.\n   332→\n   333→**CSS organization with cascade layers:**\n   334→```css\n   335→@layer reset, tokens, base, layout, components, utilities;\n   336→```\n   337→- **reset**: Normalize/reset styles\n   338→- **tokens**: Custom properties (design tokens)\n   339→- **base**: Element-level styles (body, headings, links, forms)\n   340→- **layout**: Page-level layout (CSS Grid)\n   341→- **components**: Component-specific styles (todo-item, auth-form)\n   342→- **utilities**: Helper classes (visually-hidden, etc.)\n   343→- No `!important` unless in the utilities layer for intentional overrides.\n   344→- CSS nesting is fine for component-scoped styles but avoid nesting deeper than\n   345→  2 levels.\n   346→\n   347→**Design tokens (CSS custom properties on `:root`):**\n   348→- **Spacing scale** (4px base): 4, 8, 12, 16, 24, 32, 48, 64, 96 -- encoded as\n   349→  `--space-xs` through `--space-3xl`\n   350→- **Color palette**: oklch color space for perceptual uniformity. One primary color,\n   351→  neutral gray palette (50-900), semantic colors (danger, success, warning). Most UI\n   352→  is grayscale; color is for emphasis and interaction.\n   353→- **Typography**: System font stack (`system-ui, sans-serif`). Type scale from xs to\n   354→  3xl with defined line-height. Tighter for headings, looser for body.\n   355→- **Shadows**: Three levels (sm, md, lg). Never combine shadows and borders on the\n   356→  same element.\n   357→- **Border radius**: Three sizes (sm, md, lg).\n   358→- **All values reference tokens -- no hardcoded hex values or pixel values in\n   359→  component styles.**\n   360→\n   361→**Design tokens are a prerequisite**: The token system (spacing, colors, typography,\n   362→shadows, radii) must be established and agreed upon before any feature UI work begins.\n   363→This is foundational -- without it, inconsistent one-off values accumulate from day one.\n   364→\n   365→**Design token governance**: Adding a new color, spacing value, or typography level\n   366→goes through the mob (Steve Schoger approves design token changes).\n   367→\n   368→**Design token flow**: Steve Schoger defines the visual design -> Lea encodes as CSS\n   369→custom properties -> Components reference only tokens -> Themes/dark mode reassign\n   370→properties. No build step. No JSON-to-CSS pipeline.\n   371→\n   372→**Modern CSS features:**\n   373→- `:has()` for parent-based styling (e.g., `li:has(input:checked)` for completed todos)\n   374→- Container queries where components need to respond to container size\n   375→- Logical properties (`margin-inline`, `padding-block`) for future RTL support\n   376→- `clamp()` for fluid typography\n   377→- View Transitions API for smooth HTMX swap animations\n   378→- `@supports` for graceful degradation of newer features\n   379→\n   380→**Accessibility in CSS:**\n   381→- Custom `:focus-visible` styles with at least 3:1 contrast. Never `outline: none`\n   382→  without a replacement.\n   383→- `prefers-reduced-motion`: All animations/transitions wrapped in a motion query.\n   384→  Reduced or no motion as the alternative.\n   385→- `prefers-color-scheme`: Supported if/when the team decides to add dark mode.\n   386→- Color is never the only state indicator.\n   387→\n   388→**Responsive design**: Mobile-first. Default styles target the smallest viewport;\n   389→enhancements added via `min-width` media queries. Breakpoints: mobile (default),\n   390→desktop (~1024px). A todo list should work beautifully on a phone.\n   391→\n   392→**Browser targets**: Last 2 versions of evergreen browsers (Chrome, Firefox, Safari,\n   393→Edge). No IE11. `@supports` for graceful degradation. No polyfills unless necessary.\n   394→\n   395→### TypeScript Conventions\n   396→- **No framework**: Vanilla TypeScript with DOM APIs.\n   397→- **Progressive enhancement pattern**: Feature works without JS, TypeScript enhances.\n   398→- **Event delegation**: Listeners on parent containers, not individual elements.\n   399→- **State via data attributes**: TypeScript toggles `data-*` attributes or classes;\n   400→  CSS handles all visual changes based on those.\n   401→- **No CSS-in-JS**: Styles live in CSS files. TypeScript never sets inline styles\n   402→  (except computed values like drag position).\n   403→- **Thin layer**: If a TypeScript file is getting large, we are probably doing\n   404→  something CSS or HTMX could handle.\n   405→\n   406→### Copy Standards\n   407→- **Labels**: 1-2 words when possible.\n   408→- **Error messages**: Plain language. Say what went wrong, suggest what to do next.\n   409→  \"That email isn't registered -- want to create an account?\" not \"Error: User not found.\"\n   410→- **Button labels**: Describe the action (\"Add todo\", \"Sign in\"), not vague labels\n   411→  (\"Submit\", \"OK\").\n   412→- **No happy talk**: Every word earns its place or gets cut. No introductory paragraphs\n   413→  that say nothing useful.\n   414→- **Design for scanning, not reading**: Users don't read pages, they scan. Clear\n   415→  headings, short text, prominent calls to action, no walls of text.\n   416→- **Cut the text, then cut it again**: If you wrote a paragraph, ask \"can I say this\n   417→  in half the words?\"\n   418→\n   419→### Domain Language and Modeling Conventions\n   420→- Code uses the ubiquitous language of the domain. \"Complete a task\" ->\n   421→  `complete_task()`, not `update_status()`.\n   422→- Domain types are explicit -- no primitive obsession. Every domain concept gets its\n   423→  own type, even if it is \"just a string\" or \"just a UUID\" underneath.\n   424→- Newtypes are constructed only through validated factory methods (the `parse`\n   425→  pattern). You cannot create a `TodoTitle` from an arbitrary string without going\n   426→  through validation.\n   427→- Every `is_*` boolean flag is a candidate for an enum. Ask: \"what states does this\n   428→  represent?\" and model them explicitly.\n   429→- Maintain a domain glossary in `docs/glossary.md` mapping business terms to types:\n   430→\n   431→  | Domain Term | Rust Type | Notes |\n   432→  |-------------|-----------|-------|\n   433→  | User | `User` | Authenticated user with valid credentials |\n   434→  | Email | `ValidatedEmail` | Constructed via `parse`, not `new` |\n   435→  | Todo item | `TodoItem` (enum) | `Pending` or `Completed` variant |\n   436→  | Todo title | `TodoTitle` | Non-empty, max length, validated at construction |\n   437→\n   438→### Observability\n   439→\n   440→**Structured logging with `tracing`:**\n   441→- Request ID (UUID) attached to every request via middleware.\n   442→- Span fields: `request_id`, `method`, `uri`, `status_code`.\n   443→- Application-level spans for significant operations: `register_user`,\n   444→  `authenticate`, `create_todo`, etc.\n   445→- Use `#[tracing::instrument]` for service functions.\n   446→- Structured fields on errors: what failed, why, relevant IDs.\n   447→\n   448→**Log level conventions:**\n   449→| Level | When to use |\n   450→|-------|-------------|\n   451→| `ERROR` | Something is broken, needs human attention |\n   452→| `WARN` | Unexpected but handled (e.g., invalid login attempt) |\n   453→| `INFO` | Significant business events (user registered, todo created) |\n   454→| `DEBUG` | Technical details useful for debugging |\n   455→| `TRACE` | Very verbose (request/response bodies, SQL queries) |\n   456→\n   457→### Database Conventions\n   458→- **Migrations**: SQLx migrations (`sqlx migrate`), numbered SQL files, version controlled.\n   459→- **Compile-time checked queries**: `sqlx::query!` and `sqlx::query_as!` macros.\n   460→- **Offline mode for CI**: `sqlx-data.json` generated via `cargo sqlx prepare`,\n   461→  committed to version control.\n   462→- **Connection pool**: `PgPool` shared via Axum state.\n   463→- **UUIDs for primary keys**: `uuid` type in PostgreSQL, `Uuid` in Rust.\n   464→- **Timestamps**: `timestamptz` in PostgreSQL, `chrono::DateTime<Utc>` or\n   465→  `time::OffsetDateTime` in Rust.\n   466→- **Naming conventions**: snake_case for tables and columns. Plural table names\n   467→  (`users`, `todos`).\n   468→\n   469→### Configuration Management\n   470→- Layered configuration: `base.yaml` (defaults) -> `local.yaml` (gitignored overrides)\n   471→  -> environment variables (12-factor style).\n   472→- **Fail fast**: Missing required configuration at startup panics with a clear message.\n   473→  No silent defaults for critical settings (database URL, secret keys).\n   474→- Separate configuration structs: `DatabaseSettings`, `ApplicationSettings`,\n   475→  `AuthSettings`.\n   476→\n   477→### CI/CD Quality Gates\n   478→\n   479→Every commit must pass (in order):\n   480→1. `cargo fmt --check`\n   481→2. `cargo clippy -- -D warnings`\n   482→3. `cargo test` (unit + integration)\n   483→4. `npx playwright test` (browser-based e2e)\n   484→5. `cargo audit` (dependency vulnerabilities)\n   485→\n   486→### Atomic Green Step Pipeline\n   487→\n   488→*Every change follows this pipeline. No shortcuts, no skipped steps.*\n   489→\n   490→1. **Write code** — the smallest meaningful change.\n   491→2. **`cargo fmt --check`** — fix formatting if needed.\n   492→3. **`cargo clippy -- -D warnings`** — fix warnings if needed.\n   493→4. **`cargo test`** — fix failures if needed.\n   494→5. **`npx playwright test`** — fix e2e failures if needed.\n   495→6. **`git commit`** — commit locally. **Do NOT push yet.**\n   496→7. **All 9 agents review and reach consensus** — Driver and Reviewers confirm the change\n   497→   is correct. If concerns are raised, the Driver fixes them, re-runs steps 2–6, and\n   498→   re-seeks consensus.\n   499→8. **Once 9/9 consensus → `git push`.**\n   500→9. **`gh run list --limit 1`** — verify CI completes green.\n   501→10. **Only then begin the next change.**\n   502→\n   503→Additional rules:\n   504→- **Consensus before push.** Code is reviewed locally before it reaches the remote. This\n   505→  keeps the CI wait out of the feedback loop.\n   506→- **If CI fails, fix it before writing new code.** A red CI is the team's top priority.\n   507→  No new features, no new tests, no refactoring until CI is green again.\n   508→- **One Driver at a time.** Only the designated Driver may modify files. Non-driver agents\n   509→  MUST NOT use Edit, Write, or Bash tools that modify files. Violation is treated as a\n   510→  process failure.\n   511→\n   512→### Dependency Management\n   513→\n   514→Before adding a new crate:\n   515→- Is it well-maintained? (Recent commits, responsive maintainers)\n   516→- Is it widely used? (Downloads, reverse dependencies)\n   517→- Compatible license? (MIT/Apache-2.0 preferred)\n   518→- Can we avoid it? (Prefer stdlib or existing dependencies)\n   519→\n   520→### Documentation\n   521→- **Code comments**: Only where \"why\" is not obvious from the code.\n   522→- **ADRs**: For significant technical decisions. Format: context, decision,\n   523→  consequences. Stored in `docs/adr/`.\n   524→- **Domain glossary**: `docs/glossary.md` mapping business terms to code.\n   525→- **README**: Practical -- how to set up, run tests, run the app.\n   526→\n   527→---\n   528→\n   529→## 4. Disagreement Resolution\n   530→\n   531→### In the Mob (Day-to-Day)\n   532→1. State the disagreement clearly: \"I think X, you think Y.\"\n   533→2. Each side explains their reasoning briefly (< 2 minutes each).\n   534→3. If possible, **try both and let the code decide** -- write a quick test or prototype.\n   535→4. If one approach is simpler, prefer it (smallest viable decision).\n   536→5. If still stuck after 5 minutes, the mob votes. Majority wins for day-to-day decisions.\n   537→   The dissenter can say \"I disagree but won't block.\"\n   538→\n   539→### For Significant Decisions (Consensus Protocol)\n   540→1. Any team member raises the decision point with a proposal and reasoning.\n   541→2. Each team member shares their perspective (concerns, alternatives, support).\n   542→3. Discussion continues until:\n   543→   - **Consensus**: Everyone agrees or consents (\"I can live with this\").\n   544→   - **Compromise**: A synthesized solution addresses all concerns.\n   545→   - **Stand-aside**: \"I disagree but won't block\" -- recorded and respected.\n   546→4. If no consensus after **10 rounds** of substantive discussion, **escalate to the\n   547→   project owner** with:\n   548→   - Options considered\n   549→   - Each member's position\n   550→   - Trade-offs\n   551→   - Team recommendation (if possible)\n   552→\n   553→### When to Involve the Project Owner\n   554→- Consensus deadlock after 10 rounds\n   555→- Any proposed change to MVP scope\n   556→- Questions about target user or business context the team cannot answer\n   557→- Major architectural pivots that significantly change the timeline\n   558→- Brief status updates at milestones (keep the owner informed, don't go dark)\n   559→\n   560→### Principles\n   561→- Disagree with the idea, not the person.\n   562→- Once decided, **disagree and commit** -- no undermining, no \"I told you so.\"\n   563→- Revisit decisions when new information emerges (from tests, users, or production).\n   564→- **Write it down**: Major decisions recorded as Architecture Decision Records (ADRs)\n   565→  in `docs/adr/`.\n   566→\n   567→---\n   568→\n   569→## 5. Architectural Principles\n   570→\n   571→1. **Simplicity first**: Choose the simplest approach that could work. Add complexity\n   572→   only when tests or user feedback demand it. \"Could this be simpler?\" is always a\n   573→   valid question.\n   574→2. **Server-side state**: The server is the source of truth for both data and\n   575→   presentation. The browser renders what the server sends. No client-side state\n   576→   management.\n   577→3. **Pure domain core**: Domain logic is pure functions and types with no I/O. Side\n   578→   effects live at the boundaries. This makes the domain trivially testable.\n   579→4. **Make illegal states unrepresentable**: Use the type system to prevent bugs at\n   580→   compile time. Newtypes, enums, and validated types carry proof of correctness.\n   581→5. **Production-ready from day one**: Observability, error handling, and structured\n   582→   logging from the first line of code -- not bolted on later.\n   583→6. **Accessibility is a quality, not a feature**: Every feature is accessible from the\n   584→   moment it is built. Inaccessible is broken. ~15-20% of users have some form of\n   585→   disability -- that is not an edge case.\n   586→7. **Progressive enhancement**: HTML works -> CSS makes it beautiful -> JS makes it\n   587→   delightful. Each layer enhances without being required by the layers above.\n   588→8. **Conventions over cleverness**: Follow established patterns. A login form should\n   589→   look like every other login form. Don't make the user think. Design for scanning,\n   590→   not reading. Cut unnecessary words. When in doubt, simplify.\n   591→9. **Continuous testing**: TDD keeps us honest. The compiler is our first test. We\n   592→   never skip the red step. Tests read like behavior specifications.\n   593→10. **Incremental design**: Let the design emerge from tests and feedback. Don't\n   594→    over-design upfront. Make the code a little better before adding a feature (Tidy\n   595→    First), but don't redesign the universe. Ship early, learn fast.\n   596→11. **Walking skeleton first**: Our first milestone is the thinnest possible slice\n   597→    through the entire stack -- a user can register, log in, see an empty todo list,\n   598→    add one item, and log out. Everything else builds on top.\n   599→12. **Validate at the boundary, trust the types**: Input validation happens once, at\n   600→    the system boundary. It produces typed values that carry proof of validity.\n   601→    The interior of the system trusts its own types.\n   602→\n   603→---\n   604→\n   605→## 6. Retrospective Cadence\n   606→\n   607→All team members are AI agents operating continuously. Time-based retros (weekly,\n   608→bi-weekly) do not apply. Instead, retros are triggered by events.\n   609→\n   610→- **After each feature**: Retro immediately after completing a feature. What worked?\n   611→  What didn't? What should we change?\n   612→- **After significant incidents**: If a build breaks, a major refactor goes sideways,\n   613→  or the team gets stuck for an extended period, retro after resolution.\n   614→- **Format**: Simple Start/Stop/Continue.\n   615→- **Action items**: Every retro produces at most 2-3 concrete action items. These are\n   616→  tracked and checked at the next retro.\n   617→- **Agreements are living**: These team agreements can be updated at any retro if the\n   618→  team reaches consensus.\n   619→- **Usability testing**: Aim for informal testing -- three users, 20 minutes each --\n   620→  at natural breakpoints. Even watching one person use the app for 5 minutes reveals\n   621→  more than a week of discussion.\n   622→\n   623→---\n   624→\n   625→## 7. Tooling & Repository\n   626→\n   627→### Source Control\n   628→- **Repository**: Public GitHub repository under the `jwilger` account\n   629→- **License**: MIT\n   630→- **Branching**: Work on `main` for now. Feature branches if/when the team decides\n   631→  they are needed.\n   632→\n   633→### CI/CD\n   634→- **GitHub Actions**: CI runs on every push and pull request to `main`.\n   635→- **Pipeline stages** (in order):\n   636→  1. `cargo fmt --check`\n   637→  2. `cargo clippy -- -D warnings`\n   638→  3. `cargo test`\n   639→  4. `npx playwright test`\n   640→- Rust nightly toolchain (matching the project's `rust-toolchain.toml`)\n   641→- Node.js 22 for Playwright e2e tests\n   642→- CI must pass before merging any pull request.\n   643→\n   644→### Work Tracking\n   645→- **GitHub Issues**: For tracking features, bugs, and tasks visible to the project owner.\n   646→- **Claude Task tool**: For in-progress coordination between team members during a session.\n   647→- Issues and tasks should reference each other when applicable.\n   648→\n   649→---\n   650→\n   651→## 8. Team Composition Assessment\n   652→\n   653→### Current Team (9 members)\n   654→| Name | Role | Domain |\n   655→|------|------|--------|\n   656→| Kent Beck | TDD Coach & Dev Practice Lead | TDD, XP, refactoring |\n   657→| Scott Wlaschin | Domain Architect | DDD, type-driven design, FP |\n   658→| Luca Palmieri | Lead Rust Engineer | Axum, SQLx, production Rust |\n   659→| Carson Gross | Hypermedia Architect & Frontend Lead | HTMX, hypermedia systems |\n   660→| Lea Verou | Frontend Engineer | CSS, web standards |\n   661→| Steve Schoger | UI Designer | Visual design, design systems |\n   662→| Steve Krug | UX Specialist | Usability, user advocacy |\n   663→| Heydon Pickering | Accessibility Specialist | WCAG, inclusive design |\n   664→| Marty Cagan | Product Manager | Product discovery, MVP |\n   665→\n   666→### Assessment\n   667→The current team covers all necessary disciplines for this MVP:\n   668→- **Product**: Marty Cagan\n   669→- **Design**: Steve Schoger (visual) + Steve Krug (UX) + Heydon Pickering (a11y)\n   670→- **Architecture**: Scott Wlaschin (domain) + Carson Gross (hypermedia) + Luca\n   671→  Palmieri (Rust/infra)\n   672→- **Frontend**: Carson Gross (HTMX) + Lea Verou (CSS/HTML) + Heydon Pickering\n   673→  (a11y review)\n   674→- **Backend**: Luca Palmieri + Scott Wlaschin\n   675→- **Process**: Kent Beck (TDD, mob facilitation)\n   676→\n   677→### Potential Gaps to Monitor\n   678→- **DevOps/Infrastructure**: No dedicated ops person. Luca has deployment experience\n   679→  but if CI/CD or infrastructure becomes complex, we may want to recruit.\n   680→- **Security**: Auth is in scope. Luca has experience but if we encounter complex\n   681→  security requirements, consider a security specialist.\n   682→- **QA/Testing beyond TDD**: The team practices TDD rigorously, but exploratory\n   683→  testing and load testing may need attention for production readiness.\n   684→- **Analytics/Measurement**: If we are serious about \"outcomes over output,\" we will\n   685→  eventually need to measure whether the product solves the user's problem.
